<div id="review_174456029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174456029" />
    <a title="Emma Spadoni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5585739-emma-spadoni"><img alt="Emma Spadoni" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174456029?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Spadoni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Spadoni" href="/user/show/5585739-emma-spadoni">Emma Spadoni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174456029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15985787594689940470">Julia Glass wrote the book Three Junes for mature adults, to show complications in life. This book was written in third and first person, alternating characters in a series of three books. The protagonist in the first book, titled Collies and takes place in 1989 in Greece and Scotland, is Paul McLeod but there is no true antagonist. The protagonist in the second book, titled Upright and takes place in 1995 in America and Scotland, is Paul’s son, Fenno. The antagonist would be the disease AIDS. T</span>
  <span id="freeText15985787594689940470" style="display:none">Julia Glass wrote the book Three Junes for mature adults, to show complications in life. This book was written in third and first person, alternating characters in a series of three books. The protagonist in the first book, titled Collies and takes place in 1989 in Greece and Scotland, is Paul McLeod but there is no true antagonist. The protagonist in the second book, titled Upright and takes place in 1995 in America and Scotland, is Paul’s son, Fenno. The antagonist would be the disease AIDS. The protagonist in the third book, titled Boys and takes place in 1999 in America, is Fern Olitsky. Although the book contained multiple motifs, one that was exceptionally evident was the trial of overcoming death. The purpose of this novel is to show real life situations and struggles of everyday people throughout the world. SPOILER ALERT: Puppies die and the book contains inappropriate content. We have never read another book like this. We don’t recommend this book to the everyday reader. There is a serious lack of plot, particularly in the last book. The book is slow paced and uses an extensive vocabulary that may bore and confuse average reader. The ending does not effectively wrap up the three stories. There are many flashbacks and changes of scenery which can cause confusion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15985787594689940470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6666159642165568900">I picked this book up at the library because I thought I recognized the title. It turned out to be pretty different from what I thought it was going to be, but a very interesting read about the ways love plays out among family and friends. It honestly portrays love as very complicated, making clear that those we love are often people we may not like at certain times. Also interesting and unusual for me to read, was one of the main story lines followed the life of a homosexual man. I'm not sure w</span>
  <span id="freeText6666159642165568900" style="display:none">I picked this book up at the library because I thought I recognized the title. It turned out to be pretty different from what I thought it was going to be, but a very interesting read about the ways love plays out among family and friends. It honestly portrays love as very complicated, making clear that those we love are often people we may not like at certain times. Also interesting and unusual for me to read, was one of the main story lines followed the life of a homosexual man. I'm not sure what I want to say about that, but did want to include it in my notes here, so anyone who chooses to read it isn't surprised. The book didn't deal with any moral issues I associate with this lifestyle, and if this makes sense, the homosexuality was treated as part of the identity of the character, but not what defined him. It was interesting for me to read a book where the the homosexual character was portrayed as complex and multifaceted, as opposed to having that one attribute be his sole contribution to the story. Before I box myself into too narrow of a corner with this issue, I'll stop.</span>

<div id="review_251189055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251189055" />
    <a title="Bowerbird" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1997484-bowerbird"><img alt="Bowerbird" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1235046765p2/1997484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/251189055?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bowerbird" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bowerbird" href="/user/show/1997484-bowerbird">Bowerbird</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251189055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11291462660072605157">In a way this is three interconnected books in one. Each "June" story revolves in some way round a death in the family. Because Julia Glass uses a different person's viewpoint to develop each section, one is given more understanding of the various characters. But it is Fenno, the one portrayed as the outsider who is central to the book.<br/>The story begins with Paul the father, who first features as the main character. In June 1989 the family in Scotland copes with the death of the mother figure. As</span>
  <span id="freeText11291462660072605157" style="display:none">In a way this is three interconnected books in one. Each "June" story revolves in some way round a death in the family. Because Julia Glass uses a different person's viewpoint to develop each section, one is given more understanding of the various characters. But it is Fenno, the one portrayed as the outsider who is central to the book.<br />The story begins with Paul the father, who first features as the main character. In June 1989 the family in Scotland copes with the death of the mother figure. As we meet other members of the family, we learn of their own and their parents' expectations and hopes for them.<br />The middle June is centred mainly in New York, where Fenno speaks directly to us. Then the final June is seen chiefly through Fern's perspective.<br />I did not find this technique too confusing generally. I did feel however that at times it made the storylines a bit 'clunky'. Also, when I came to fhe final June, I didn't immediately recall where we had met Fern. <br />If I could have given this book three and a half stars I would have done so. I have already started to read my second Julia Glass book which just proves that I do like her writing. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11291462660072605157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read09">read09</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41813356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17368660758400443924">I kept putting this book down, but only because I was going to be sad when it ended. There isn't anything life changing here, just characters I really grew to care about, interesting storylines about family and identity, and some of it was set in Scotland, how can you lose. I'm just happy to see that Julia Glass has written more since this, which was her first novel and went on to win the National Book Award. I hope it wasn't a fluke!<br/><br/>"All I did for years, all I remember doing, was practice. Prac</span>
  <span id="freeText17368660758400443924" style="display:none">I kept putting this book down, but only because I was going to be sad when it ended. There isn't anything life changing here, just characters I really grew to care about, interesting storylines about family and identity, and some of it was set in Scotland, how can you lose. I'm just happy to see that Julia Glass has written more since this, which was her first novel and went on to win the National Book Award. I hope it wasn't a fluke!<br /><br />"All I did for years, all I remember doing, was practice. Practice: such a limp word for the context. You do not, if you are serious, practice your instrument. You flay, eviscerate, excoriate the thing until it surrenders its thingness, until its carapace cracks open and it bleeds. Even a voice. You belabor it until any sound but the sound of that instrument is, to your ears, gelatinous babble." -Mal from Three Junes by Julia Glass (144)<br /><br />"'I hate it when people talk about twists of fate,' Anna liked to say. 'When it comes to life, we spin our own yarn, and where we end up is really, in fact, where we always intended to be.'" -Three Junes (286)</span>

<div id="review_1695316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1695316" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/118215-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181085989p2/118215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1695316?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/118215-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1695316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2578067122124633448">Sometimes extraordinary books are about extraordinary things, and sometimes they are about regular people. This is an extraordinary book about one Scottish family, a normal family, if, of course, there is actually any such thing as normal, and assuming normal includes a little bit of human mystery and tragedy. <br/>Three Junes starts with the death of the mother of the family, and explores the stories of her husband, her three sons, (two married in Britain, one in New York during the AIDs crisis of t</span>
  <span id="freeText2578067122124633448" style="display:none">Sometimes extraordinary books are about extraordinary things, and sometimes they are about regular people. This is an extraordinary book about one Scottish family, a normal family, if, of course, there is actually any such thing as normal, and assuming normal includes a little bit of human mystery and tragedy. <br />Three Junes starts with the death of the mother of the family, and explores the stories of her husband, her three sons, (two married in Britain, one in New York during the AIDs crisis of the 1980s.) It's beautifully written; this spring I had an infection brought on by the flu, plus antibiotics that made me sick, but I still couldn't put this book down.<br />I only have one nitpicky comment - in section two, after a death takes place in Greece, and we hear that a cremation is planned, I couldn't help but mutter that hey, cremation was outlawed in Greece until recently. The incredible smallness of this one criticism should tell you how much I enjoyed this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2578067122124633448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2606541447" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606541447" />
    <a title="Elinor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11258836-elinor"><img alt="Elinor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503239631p2/11258836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2606541447?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elinor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elinor" href="/user/show/11258836-elinor">Elinor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2606541447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4111676696525450422">The title implies that this is the story of three women named June. In fact, it refers to three months in three different years of the lives of three very different people. It has a richly described setting with nuanced characters and the plot is quite intriguing. The first section is about a Scottish widower who is trying to heal his grief on a Greek holiday. The second section concerns his eldest son, Fenno, who moves to New York, opens a bookstore specializing in bird books called Plume, and </span>
  <span id="freeText4111676696525450422" style="display:none">The title implies that this is the story of three women named June. In fact, it refers to three months in three different years of the lives of three very different people. It has a richly described setting with nuanced characters and the plot is quite intriguing. The first section is about a Scottish widower who is trying to heal his grief on a Greek holiday. The second section concerns his eldest son, Fenno, who moves to New York, opens a bookstore specializing in bird books called Plume, and wrestles with his gay lifestyle in the era of AIDS. The third section describes a passage in the life of a young woman who has come into contact with both the father and son. Fenno has the largest role in this novel, but I found him the least likeable character. However, this first novel is an extremely well-written work of literary fiction and it deserved to win the 2002 National Book Award. I plan to read one of her later novels to see how it measures up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4111676696525450422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BD+Kb1Vdb0gHZuN49Abt+8BCrj3hrTJ8to+shu+sH097bN3/5zWp8yrrRIINUZJdz+saQR+PASbSt5JbHvSKMw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jCag66+eWC9lBiAnCGs799Ufh1j45h/DXd+eI34jzdfzdfd7HfaelEiLh93xPERR2rYzJAbELJk556D+j3tYqw==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9972.Julia_Glass">About Julia Glass</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/9972.Julia_Glass"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1370348112p3/9972.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/9972.Julia_Glass">Julia Glass
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
616
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13903328782346921169">Julia Glass is the author of <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227593.Three_Junes' title='Three Junes by Julia Glass' rel='nofollow noopener'>Three Junes</a>
</i>, which won the 2002 National Book Award for Fiction, and <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27646.The_Whole_World_Over' title='The Whole World Over by Julia Glass' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Whole World Over</a>
</i>. She has received fellowships from the National Endowment for the Arts, the New York Foundation for the Arts, and the Radcliffe Institute for Advanced Study. Her short fiction has won several prizes, including the Tobias Wolff Award and the Pirate's Alley Faulkner Society </span>
  <span id="freeText13903328782346921169" style="display:none">Julia Glass is the author of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227593.Three_Junes" title="Three Junes by Julia Glass" rel="nofollow noopener">Three Junes</a>
</i>, which won the 2002 National Book Award for Fiction, and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27646.The_Whole_World_Over" title="The Whole World Over by Julia Glass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Whole World Over</a>
</i>. She has received fellowships from the National Endowment for the Arts, the New York Foundation for the Arts, and the Radcliffe Institute for Advanced Study. Her short fiction has won several prizes, including the Tobias Wolff Award and the Pirate's Alley Faulkner Society Medal for the Best Novella. She lives with her family in Massachusetts.<br /><br />Her new novel, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3078805.I_See_You_Everywhere" title="I See You Everywhere by Julia Glass" rel="nofollow noopener">I See You Everywhere</a>
</i> is scheduled for release October 14, 2008.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13903328782346921169" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
